============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK1)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A + c3*_w*cos(log(A + c4))
Candidate formulas: 90

GT is the fixed function of \(A\) (no \(t\) dependence):
\[
f(A)= -0.7725880991\,A^2 -0.7725880991\,A + 0.7402077580\cos(\log(A+1)).
\]
So any matching candidate must (i) be independent of \(t\), (ii) contain exactly a quadratic polynomial part with those coefficients, and (iii) reproduce the specific non-polynomial term \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) (not \(\sin\), not \(\log\), not \(\exp\), not \(\cos(\log(\text{something else}))\)), up to choosing constants.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether its functional form can be tuned to equal \(f(A)\) for all \(A\).

1. \(c0 + c1(A+c2)^2 + c3\sin(c4\log(c5 e^{Ac6}+1)+c7)\): has \(\sin(\log(1+c5 e^{Ac6}))\), not \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). Also inside log is exponential in \(A\), not linear \(A+1\). Cannot match.
2. \(c0A^2+c1A+c2+c3e^{Ac4}+c5e^{Ac6}\): exponentials cannot become \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) for all \(A\). No.
3. \(c0\sin(c1A+c2)+c3e^{c4|A|}+c5\): wrong nonlinearity types. No.
4. \(c0A^2+c1A+\frac{c3A^{c2}}{A^{c2}+c4}+c5+c6\log(c7A+1)\): has rational-in-\(A^{c2}\) and \(\log\) term, not \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). No.
5. \(c0+c1e^{Ac2}+c3\sin(c4A+c5)\): no.
6. \(c0+c1(A+c2)^{c3}+c4\frac{|A+c5|^{c6}}{c7+|A+c5|^{c6}}\): no cosine-log. No.
7. \(c0+c1e^{Ac2}+c3\log(c4e^{c5(A+c6)^{c7}}+1)\): log/exp composition, not cosine-log. No.
8. \(c0+\frac{c1}{c2A+c3}+c4(c5+|A|)^{c6}e^{c7|A|}\): no.
9. includes \(t\) in exponent inside log; GT has no \(t\). Only way is set that whole term to 0 (e.g., \(c4=0\)), but then remaining is \(c0+c1/(c2A+c3)\), not GT. No.
10. sum of sines with log(exp(|A|)); not \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). No.

GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A + c3*_w*cos(log(A + c4))

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.7726*A² - 0.7726*A + 0.7402*cos(log(A + 1))`

Key features of GT:
- A quadratic polynomial: `-0.7726*A² - 0.7726*A`
- A `cos(log(A+1))` term with coefficient ~0.7402
- No dependence on `t`

Let me analyze candidates systematically. I'll focus on:
1. Can the candidate produce the `cos(log(A+1))` term?
2. Can it produce the quadratic polynomial part?
3. Does it have unwanted `t` dependence that can't be zeroed?

**Key identity needed:** `cos(log(A+1))` is a very specific transcendental function. It cannot be represented by exponentials, simple logs, polynomials, or simple trigonometric functions of A.

Let me check which candidates have the right structure:

**Candidates with `sin(c*log(c*exp(A*c) + 1) + c)` type terms:**
This is promising because `sin(log(exp(0) + 1) + phase)` with `c6=0` gives `sin(log(1+1)+phase)` which is constant. But if we set the coefficient of A inside exp to 0, we get `sin(c4*log(c5+1) + c7)` which is just a constant.

Wait - let me reconsider. If `c5*exp(A*c6) + 1` and we want `log(A+1)`, we need a different approach. `exp(A*c6)` can't become `A+1` inside a log.

Actually, let me reconsider the structure `sin(c4*log(c5*exp(A*c6) + 1) + c7)`:
- If c6 is very small, by Taylor expansion... but NO, we need EXACT equivalence.

**Can `log(c*exp(f(A)) + 1)` equal `log(A+1)`?**
We need `c*exp(f(A)) + 1 = (A+1)^k` for some k. If `f(A) = 0` (c6=0), then `log(c5+1)` is constant.

Actually, `log(A+1) = log(exp(log(A+1)))`. So if we could write `c5*exp(A*c6) = A`, that's impossible for all A.

**Candidate 1:** `c0 + c1*(A+c2)² + c3*sin(c4*log(c5*exp(A*c6)+1) + c7)`
The quadratic part works. For the sin term: we need `sin(c4*log(c5*exp(A*c6)+1)+c7) = cos(log(A+1))`. This requires `log(c5*exp(A*c6)+1) = log(A+1)`, i.e., `c5*exp(A*c6)+1 = A+1`, i.e., `c5*exp(A*c6) = A`. This can't hold for all A.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 27:** `A²*c0 + A*c1 + c2 + c3*sin(c4*log(c5*exp(A*c6)+1) + c7)` - Same issue.
